4. WRITE /workspace/profile_elkan.py
#!/usr/bin/env python
"""
Profile K-Means Elkan algorithm to identify bottlenecks.
"""

import numpy as np
import cProfile
import pstats
import io
from sklearn.cluster._kmeans import _kmeans_single_elkan
from sklearn.utils.extmath import row_norms
from sklearn.utils import check_random_state
from sklearn.utils.validation import _check_sample_weight
from sklearn.cluster._kmeans import _kmeans_plusplus

def profile_elkan():
    """Profile the K-Means Elkan algorithm."""
    n_samples = 10000
    n_features = 50
    n_clusters = 50
    max_iter = 50
    random_state_val = 42

    # Generate test data
    rng = np.random.RandomState(random_state_val)
    X = rng.randn(n_samples, n_features).astype(np.float64)
    X = np.ascontiguousarray(X)

    # Prepare data
    random_state = check_random_state(random_state_val)
    sample_weight = _check_sample_weight(None, X, dtype=X.dtype)

    # Center the data
    X_mean = X.mean(axis=0)
    X = X - X_mean

    # Precompute squared norms
    x_squared_norms = row_norms(X, squared=True)

    # Initialize centers
    centers_init, _ = _kmeans_plusplus(
        X, n_clusters, x_squared_norms=x_squared_norms,
        sample_weight=sample_weight, random_state=random_state
    )

    # Profile the main function
    pr = cProfile.Profile()
    pr.enable()

    labels, inertia, centers, n_iter = _kmeans_single_elkan(
        X,
        sample_weight,
        centers_init.copy(),
        max_iter=max_iter,
        verbose=False,
        tol=1e-4,
        n_threads=1,
    )

    pr.disable()

    # Print results
    s = io.StringIO()
    ps = pstats.Stats(pr, stream=s).sort_stats('cumulative')
    ps.print_stats(30)
    print(s.getvalue())

    return labels, inertia, centers, n_iter

if __name__ == "__main__":
    profile_elkan()

"""Optimized K-means Elkan single run implementation.

Optimizations applied:
1. Vectorized bounds update using NumPy operations instead of Python loops
2. Optimized center half distances computation
"""

import numpy as np
import scipy.sparse as sp

from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import euclidean_distances
from sklearn.cluster._k_means_common import _inertia_dense, _inertia_sparse
from sklearn.cluster._k_means_elkan import (
    elkan_iter_chunked_dense,
    elkan_iter_chunked_sparse,
    init_bounds_dense,
    init_bounds_sparse,
)


def _kmeans_single_elkan_optimized(
    X,
    sample_weight,
    centers_init,
    max_iter=300,
    verbose=False,
    tol=1e-4,
    n_threads=1,
):
    """A single run of k-means elkan, assumes preparation completed prior.

    Optimized version with vectorized bounds updates.

    Parameters
    ----------
    X : {ndarray, sparse matrix} of shape (n_samples, n_features)
        The observations to cluster. If sparse matrix, must be in CSR format.

    sample_weight : array-like of shape (n_samples,)
        The weights for each observation in X.

    centers_init : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features)
        The initial centers.

    max_iter : int, default=300
        Maximum number of iterations of the k-means algorithm to run.

    verbose : bool, default=False
        Verbosity mode.

    tol : float, default=1e-4
        Relative tolerance with regards to Frobenius norm of the difference
        in the cluster centers of two consecutive iterations to declare
        convergence.

    n_threads : int, default=1
        The number of OpenMP threads to use for the computation.

    Returns
    -------
    labels : ndarray of shape (n_samples,)
        label[i] is the code or index of the centroid the
        i'th observation i
... (truncated)

#!/usr/bin/env python
"""
Benchmark script for comparing baseline and optimized K-Means Elkan implementations.
"""

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace')

import numpy as np
import time
from sklearn.cluster._kmeans import _kmeans_single_elkan
from sklearn.utils.extmath import row_norms
from sklearn.utils import check_random_state
from sklearn.utils.validation import _check_sample_weight
from sklearn.cluster._kmeans import _kmeans_plusplus

from optimized import _kmeans_single_elkan_optimized


def run_benchmark(func, X, sample_weight, centers_init, max_iter, n_threads, n_iterations=5):
    """Run benchmark for a given function."""
    times = []
    n_iters = []
    inertias = []
    for _ in range(n_iterations):
        start = time.perf_counter()
        labels, inertia, centers, n_iter = func(
            X,
            sample_weight,
            centers_init.copy(),
            max_iter=max_iter,
            verbose=False,
            tol=1e-4,
            n_threads=n_threads,
        )
        elapsed = time.perf_counter() - start
        times.append(elapsed)
        n_iters.append(n_iter)
        inertias.append(inertia)

    return np.mean(times), np.std(times), n_iters[-1], inertias[-1], labels


def main():
    # Parameters to get close to 0.182s baseline

    n_features = 50

    X = X - X_mean

    )

    labels = np.full(n_samples, -1, dtype=np.int32)

10. WRITE /workspace/optimize_distances.py
#!/usr/bin/env python
"""
Test different ways to compute pairwise distances between centers.
"""

import numpy as np
import time
from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import euclidean_distances
from scipy.spatial.distance import cdist
from sklearn.utils.extmath import row_norms


def test_distance_methods():
    """Compare different methods for computing center distances."""
    n_clusters = 50
    n_features = 50
    n_iterations = 100

    rng = np.random.RandomState(42)
    centers = rng.randn(n_clusters, n_features).astype(np.float64)
    centers = np.ascontiguousarray(centers)

    # Method 1: sklearn euclidean_distances
    t0 = time.perf_counter()
    for _ in range(n_iterations):
        dist1 = euclidean_distances(centers)
    t_sklearn = (time.perf_counter() - t0) / n_iterations
    print(f"sklearn euclidean_distances: {t_sklearn*1000:.3f} ms")

    # Method 2: scipy cdist
    t0 = time.perf_counter()
    for _ in range(n_iterations):
        dist2 = cdist(centers, centers, metric='euclidean')
    t_scipy = (time.perf_counter() - t0) / n_iterations
    print(f"scipy cdist: {t_scipy*1000:.3f} ms")

    # Method 3: Custom with precomputed norms
    centers_squared_norms = row_norms(centers, squared=True)
    t0 = time.perf_counter()
    for _ in range(n_iterations):
        # D^2 = ||a||^2 + ||b||^2 - 2 * a.b
        dist3_sq = centers_squared_norms[:, np.newaxis] + centers_squared_norms[np.newaxis, :] - 2 * np.dot(centers, centers.T)
        np.maximum(dist3_sq, 0, out=dist3_sq)  # Handle numerical errors
        dist3 = np.sqrt(dist3_sq)
    t_custom = (time.perf_counter() - t0) / n_iterations
    print(f"Custom with precomputed norms: {t_custom*1000:.3f} ms")

    t0 = time.perf_counter()

def _fast_euclidean_pairwise(centers, centers_squared_norms=None, out=None):
    """Compute pairwise Euclidean distances between centers efficiently.

    Uses the formula: D^2 = ||a||^2 + ||b||^2 - 2 * a.b

    Parameters
    ----------
    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features)
        The cluster centers.

    centers_squared_norms : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), optional
        Precomputed squared norms of centers. Computed if not provided.

    out : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), optional
        Output buffer for the distance matrix.

    Returns
    -------
    distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters)
        Pairwise Euclidean distances.
    """
    n_clusters = centers.shape[0]

    if centers_squared_norms is None:
        centers_squared_norms = row_norms(centers, squared=True)

    if out is None:
        out = np.empty((n_clusters, n_clusters), dtype=centers.dtype)

    # D^2 = ||a||^2 + ||b||^2 - 2 * a.b
    np.dot(centers, centers.T, out=out)
    out *= -2
    out += centers_squared_norms[:, np.newaxis]
    out += centers_squared_norms[np.newaxis, :]

    # Handle numerical errors (distances should be non-negative)

import numpy as np
import time
import json

from optimized import _kmeans_single_elkan_optimized


def run_benchmark(func, X, sample_weight, centers_init, max_iter, n_threads, n_iterations=5):
    """Run benchmark for a given function."""
    times = []
    for _ in range(n_iterations):
        start = time.perf_counter()
        labels, inertia, centers, n_iter = func(
            X,
            sample_weight,
            centers_init.copy(),
            max_iter=max_iter,
            verbose=False,
            tol=1e-4,
            n_threads=n_threads,
        )
        elapsed = time.perf_counter() - start
        times.append(elapsed)

    return np.mean(times), np.std(times), labels, inertia
